2.6    Section 1. APPROPRIATIONS.‚Äã

2.7        The sums shown in the columns marked "Appropriations" are added to or, if shown in‚Äã
2.8    parentheses, subtracted from the appropriations in Laws 2023, chapter 63, article 9, to the‚Äã
2.9    agencies and for the purposes specified in this article. The appropriations are from the‚Äã
2.10   general fund, or another named fund, and are available for the fiscal years indicated for‚Äã
2.11   each purpose. The figures "2024" and "2025" used in this article mean that the addition to‚Äã
2.12   or subtraction from the appropriation listed under them is available for the fiscal year ending‚Äã
2.13   June 30, 2024, or June 30, 2025, respectively. "The first year" is fiscal year 2024. "The‚Äã
2.14   second year" is fiscal year 2025. Supplemental appropriations and reductions to‚Äã
2.15   appropriations for the fiscal year ending June 30, 2024, are effective the day following final‚Äã
2.16   enactment.‚Äã

8.1                                            ARTICLE 2‚Äã
8.2                                       CANNABIS POLICY‚Äã


8.3      Section 1. Minnesota Statutes 2023 Supplement, section 3.9224, subdivision 1, is amended‚Äã
8.4    to read:‚Äã

8.5        Subdivision 1. Definitions. (a) As used in this section, the following terms have the‚Äã
8.6    meanings given.‚Äã

8.7        (b) "Medical cannabis law" or "medical cannabis program" means the regulatory‚Äã
8.8    framework for cultivation, production, distribution, and sale of cannabis to qualifying‚Äã
8.9    patients for therapeutic use in the treatment of a qualifying condition.‚Äã

8.10       (c) "Medical cannabis flower" means cannabis flower approved for sale under the medical‚Äã
8.11   cannabis law of a Minnesota Tribal government or under a compact entered into under this‚Äã
8.12   section.‚Äã

8.13       (d) "Medical cannabis product" means a cannabis product approved for sale under the‚Äã
8.14   medical cannabis law of a Minnesota Tribal government or under a compact entered into‚Äã
8.15   under this section.‚Äã

8.16       (e) "Medical cannabis business" means a medical cannabis cultivator, processor, or‚Äã
8.17   retailer business with a medical cannabis endorsement.‚Äã

8.18       (f) "Medical cannabis industry" means every item, product, person, process, action,‚Äã
8.19   business, or other thing or activity related to medical cannabis flower or medical cannabis‚Äã
8.20   products and subject to regulation under the law of a Minnesota Tribal government or under‚Äã
8.21   a compact entered into under this section.‚Äã

8.22       (g) "Cannabis product" means any of the following:‚Äã

8.23       (1) cannabis concentrate;‚Äã

8.24       (2) a product infused with cannabinoids, whether artificially derived, or extracted or‚Äã
8.25   derived from cannabis plants or cannabis flower, including but not limited to‚Äã
8.26   tetrahydrocannabinol; or‚Äã

8.27       (3) any other product that contains cannabis concentrate.‚Äã

8.28       (h) "Minnesota Tribal governments" means the following federally recognized Indian‚Äã
8.29   Tribes located in Minnesota:‚Äã

8.30       (1) Bois Forte Band;‚Äã

8.31       (2) Fond Du Lac Band;‚Äã



       Article 2 Section 1.‚Äã                         8‚Äã
       HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


9.1        (3) Grand Portage Band;‚Äã

9.2        (4) Leech Lake Band;‚Äã

9.3        (5) Mille Lacs Band;‚Äã

9.4        (6) White Earth Band;‚Äã

9.5        (7) Red Lake Nation;‚Äã

9.6        (8) Lower Sioux Indian Community;‚Äã

9.7        (9) Prairie Island Indian Community;‚Äã

9.8        (10) Shakopee Mdewakanton Sioux Community; and‚Äã

9.9        (11) Upper Sioux Indian Community.‚Äã

9.10       (i) "Tribal medical cannabis business" means a medical cannabis business licensed by‚Äã
9.11   a Minnesota Tribal government, including the business categories identified in paragraph‚Äã
9.12   (e), as well as any others that may be provided under the law of a Minnesota Tribal‚Äã
9.13   government.‚Äã

9.14       (j) "Tribally regulated land" means:‚Äã

9.15       (1) all land held in trust by the United States for the benefit of a Minnesota Tribal‚Äã
9.16   government ("trust land");‚Äã

9.17       (2) all land held by a Minnesota Tribal government in restricted fee status; and‚Äã

9.18       (3) all land within the exterior boundaries of the reservation of a Minnesota Tribal‚Äã
9.19   government that is subject to the civil regulatory jurisdiction of the Tribal government. For‚Äã
9.20   the purposes of this section, land that is subject to the civil regulatory jurisdiction of the‚Äã
9.21   Tribal government includes:‚Äã

9.22       (i) trust land, or fee land held, including leased land, by the Tribe, entities organized‚Äã
9.23   under Tribal law, or individual Indians; and‚Äã

9.24       (ii) land held, including leased land, by non-Indian entities or individuals who consent‚Äã
9.25   to the civil regulation of the Tribal government or are otherwise subject to such regulation‚Äã
9.26   under federal law.‚Äã

9.27       EFFECTIVE DATE. This section is effective the day following final enactment.‚Äã

10.1      Sec. 2. Minnesota Statutes 2023 Supplement, section 15A.0815, subdivision 2, is amended‚Äã

20.11       (2) sells an edible cannabinoid product knowing that the product does not comply with‚Äã
20.12   the applicable testing, packaging, or labeling requirements; or‚Äã

20.13       (3) sells an edible cannabinoid product to a person under the age of 21, except that it is‚Äã
20.14   an affirmative defense to a charge under this clause if the defendant proves by a‚Äã
20.15   preponderance of the evidence that the defendant reasonably and in good faith relied on‚Äã
20.16   proof of age as described in subdivision 5c.‚Äã

20.17       EFFECTIVE DATE. This section is effective July 1, 2024.‚Äã

62.5    day care, residential treatment facility, or an attraction within a public park that is regularly‚Äã
62.6    used by minors, including a playground or athletic field.‚Äã

62.7        (d) The office shall work with local units of government to:‚Äã

62.8        (1) develop model ordinances for reasonable restrictions on the time, place, and manner‚Äã
62.9    of the operation of a cannabis business;‚Äã

62.10       (2) develop standardized forms and procedures for the issuance of a retail registration‚Äã
62.11   pursuant to section 342.22; and‚Äã

62.12       (3) develop model policies and procedures for the performance of compliance checks‚Äã
62.13   required under section 342.22.‚Äã

62.14       (e) If a local unit of government is conducting studies or has authorized a study to be‚Äã
62.15   conducted or has held or has scheduled a hearing for the purpose of considering adoption‚Äã
62.16   or amendment of reasonable restrictions on the time, place, and manner of the operation of‚Äã
62.17   a cannabis business, the governing body of the local unit of government may adopt an‚Äã
62.18   interim ordinance applicable to all or part of its jurisdiction for the purpose of protecting‚Äã
62.19   the planning process and the health, safety, and welfare of its citizens. Before adopting the‚Äã
62.20   interim ordinance, the governing body must hold a public hearing. The interim ordinance‚Äã
62.21   may regulate, restrict, or prohibit the operation of a cannabis business within the jurisdiction‚Äã
62.22   or a portion thereof until January 1, 2025.‚Äã

62.23       (f) Within 30 days of receiving a copy of an application from the office, a local unit of‚Äã
62.24   government shall certify on a form provided by the office whether a proposed cannabis‚Äã
62.25   business complies with local zoning ordinances and, if applicable, whether the proposed‚Äã
62.26   business complies with the state fire code and building code. The office may not issue a‚Äã
62.27   license if a the local unit of government informs the office that the cannabis business does‚Äã
62.28   not meet local zoning and land use laws. If the local unit of government does not provide‚Äã
62.29   the certification to the office within 30 days of receiving a copy of an application from the‚Äã
62.30   office, the office may issue a license.‚Äã

62.31       (g) Upon receipt of an application for a license issued under this chapter, the office shall‚Äã
62.32   contact the local unit of government in which the business would be located and provide‚Äã
62.33   the local unit of government with 30 days in which to provide input on the application. The‚Äã
62.34   local unit of government may provide the office with any additional information it believes‚Äã


        Article 2 Sec. 64.‚Äã                            62‚Äã
        HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                    BD               H4757-4‚Äã


63.1    is relevant to the office's decision on whether to issue a license, including but not limited‚Äã
63.2    to identifying concerns about the proposed location of a cannabis business or sharing public‚Äã
63.3    information about an applicant.‚Äã

63.4        (h) (g) The office by rule shall establish an expedited complaint process to receive,‚Äã
63.5    review, and respond to complaints made by a local unit of government about a cannabis‚Äã
63.6    business. Complaints may include alleged violations of local ordinances or other alleged‚Äã
63.7    violations. At a minimum, the expedited complaint process shall require the office to provide‚Äã
63.8    an initial response to the complaint within seven days and perform any necessary inspections‚Äã
63.9    within 30 days. Nothing in this paragraph prohibits a local unit of government from enforcing‚Äã
63.10   a local ordinance. If a local unit of government notifies the office that a cannabis business‚Äã
63.11   other than a cannabis retailer, cannabis microbusiness or cannabis mezzobusiness with a‚Äã
63.12   retail operations endorsement, cannabis mezzobusiness, lower-potency hemp edible retailer,‚Äã
63.13   medical cannabis retailer, or medical cannabis combination business operating a retail‚Äã
63.14   location poses an immediate threat to the health or safety of the public, the office must‚Äã
63.15   respond within one business day and may take any action described in section 342.19 or‚Äã
63.16   342.21.‚Äã

63.17       (i) (h) A local government unit that issues a cannabis retailer registration under section‚Äã

63.19   mezzobusinesses with a retail operations endorsement, and cannabis microbusinesses with‚Äã
63.20   a retail operations endorsement to no fewer than one registration for every 12,500 residents.‚Äã

63.22   within the county is not obligated to register a cannabis business.‚Äã

63.23       (k) (j) Nothing in this section shall prohibit a local government unit from allowing‚Äã
63.24   licensed cannabis retailers in excess of the minimums set in paragraph (i) (h).‚Äã

63.26   any cannabis business to operate in Indian country, as defined in United States Code, title‚Äã
63.27   18, section 1151, of a Minnesota Tribal government without the consent of the Tribal‚Äã
63.28   government.‚Äã

71.27   retail operations endorsement that a local unit of government imposes or adopts pursuant‚Äã

71.30   that the issuance of the license would be inconsistent with the goals in subdivision 1a.‚Äã




        Article 2 Sec. 65.‚Äã                            71‚Äã

72.1        (e) Nothing in this subdivision prohibits a city or county from applying for a cannabis‚Äã
72.2    retail license subject to the requirements and procedure applicable to all other applicants.‚Äã

72.3        Subd. 8. Reconsideration. If the office denies an application or denies final authorization‚Äã
72.4    and does not issue a license after granting preliminary license approval, the applicant may‚Äã
72.5    seek reconsideration from the office. A decision by the office on a request for reconsideration‚Äã
72.6    is final.‚Äã

72.7        Subd. 9. Retention. (a) If the office holds a lottery as provided in subdivision 4, the‚Äã
72.8    office must retain the applications of any applicant not selected in the lottery for one year.‚Äã
72.9    The office must consider a retained application during any licensing periods that begin‚Äã
72.10   within the year and, except as otherwise provided in this subdivision, the office must treat‚Äã
72.11   a retained application as if the application were submitted during the licensing period.‚Äã

72.12       (b) At the beginning of a subsequent licensing period, the applicant may amend an‚Äã
72.13   application or provide additional information to the office. The office may request additional‚Äã
72.14   information from any applicant whose application is retained to determine if the applicant‚Äã
72.15   meets the requirements for a subsequent licensing period. If the applicant does not provide‚Äã
72.16   the requested information to the office within 14 calendar days of the office's request, the‚Äã
72.17   office may deny the application.‚Äã

72.18       (c) The office must not charge an additional application fee to an applicant whose‚Äã
72.19   application was retained by the office.‚Äã

72.20       (d) An applicant may withdraw a retained application at any time. If the applicant‚Äã
72.21   withdraws a retained application, the applicant may submit a new application during a‚Äã
72.22   licensing period. An applicant who submits a new application must pay the applicable‚Äã
72.23   application fee.‚Äã

72.24       (e) The office may disqualify an application from retention if the office could deny the‚Äã
72.25   application under subdivision 3, paragraph (a).‚Äã

72.26       Subd. 10. Revocation or expiration of preliminary approval. (a) A preliminary license‚Äã
72.27   approval expires after 18 months unless the office revokes the preliminary license approval‚Äã
72.28   or grants an extension. The office may grant a onetime extension of up to six months if an‚Äã
72.29   applicant has made good faith efforts to convert a preliminary license approval into a license.‚Äã
72.30   The office must not issue a license to an applicant whose preliminary license approval has‚Äã
72.31   expired.‚Äã

72.32       (b) If the office determines that an applicant is not eligible for a license, the office may‚Äã
72.33   revoke a preliminary license approval.‚Äã

75.26   has not been granted.‚Äã

81.12     Sec. 76. [342.185] TRUE PARTY OF INTEREST.‚Äã

81.13       Subdivision 1. Definitions. (a) As used in this section, the following terms have the‚Äã
81.14   meanings given.‚Äã

81.15       (b) "Control" means the power to independently order or direct the management,‚Äã
81.16   managers, or policies of a cannabis business.‚Äã

81.17       (c) "Financial institution" means any bank, mutual savings bank, consumer loan company,‚Äã
81.18   credit union, savings and loan association, trust company, or other lending institution under‚Äã
81.19   the jurisdiction of the Minnesota Department of Commerce, the United States Department‚Äã
81.20   of Commerce, or both.‚Äã

81.21       (d) "Financier" means any person that:‚Äã

81.22       (1) is not a financial institution or government entity;‚Äã

81.23       (2) provides money as a gift, grant, or loan to an applicant for a cannabis business license,‚Äã
81.24   a cannabis business, or both; and‚Äã

81.25       (3) expects to be repaid for the money provided, with or without reasonable interest.‚Äã

81.26       (e) "Gross profit" means sales minus the cost of goods sold.‚Äã

81.27       (f) "Revenue" means the income generated from the sale of goods and services associated‚Äã
81.28   with the main operations of a business before any costs or expenses have been deducted.‚Äã

83.5        Subd. 2. Application number limitations. An individual may not be a true party of‚Äã

83.23   not enter into an intellectual property agreement with another cannabis business if a single‚Äã
83.24   entity could not hold licenses for both types of cannabis business.‚Äã

83.28   directly involved in the loaning of money, has been disclosed to the office as a true party‚Äã
83.29   of interest.‚Äã

83.30       Subd. 7. Disclosure requirements. An applicant for a cannabis business license and‚Äã
83.31   cannabis business license holders must disclose all true parties of interest. Applicants and‚Äã
83.32   license holders have a continuing duty to notify the office of any change in true parties of‚Äã
83.33   interest in the form and manner specified by the office.‚Äã

134.7      Sec. 148. LICENSE PREAPPROVAL.‚Äã

134.8        Subdivision 1. Establishment. (a) Prior to the adoption of initial rules pursuant to‚Äã
134.9    Minnesota Statutes, section 342.02, subdivision 5, the Office of Cannabis Management may‚Äã
134.10   establish a license preapproval process for applicants who meet the requirements in Minnesota‚Äã
134.11   Statutes, section 342.17.‚Äã

134.12       (b) The office may issue up to the following number of license preapprovals for the‚Äã
134.13   following types of licenses:‚Äã

134.14       (1) cannabis microbusiness licenses, 100;‚Äã

134.15       (2) cannabis mezzobusiness licenses, 25;‚Äã

134.16       (3) cannabis cultivator licenses, 13;‚Äã

134.17       (4) cannabis manufacturer licenses, six;‚Äã

134.18       (5) cannabis retailer licenses, 38;‚Äã

134.19       (6) cannabis wholesaler licenses, 20;‚Äã

134.20       (7) cannabis transporter licenses, 20;‚Äã

134.21       (8) cannabis testing facility licenses, 50; and‚Äã

134.22       (9) cannabis delivery service licenses, ten.‚Äã

134.23       (c) A license preapproval remains valid for 18 months from the date that the office adopts‚Äã
134.24   initial rules pursuant to Minnesota Statutes, section 342.02, subdivision 5, unless the office‚Äã
134.25   revokes the license preapproval or grants an extension. The office may grant a onetime‚Äã
134.26   extension of up to six months if an applicant has made good faith efforts to convert a license‚Äã
134.27   preapproval into a license. The office must not issue a license to an applicant whose license‚Äã
134.28   preapproval has expired.‚Äã




         Article 2 Sec. 148.‚Äã                            134‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                   BD                H4757-4‚Äã


135.1        Subd. 2. Eligibility; social equity applicants. Only a social equity applicant who meets‚Äã
135.2    the requirements in Minnesota Statutes, section 342.17, is eligible for license preapproval.‚Äã

135.3        Subd. 3. Preapproval period. (a) The office must announce the commencement of a‚Äã
135.4    license preapproval application period at least 14 days before the date that the office begins‚Äã
135.5    to accept applications. The announcement must include:‚Äã

135.6        (1) the types of licenses that will be available for preapproval during the license‚Äã
135.7    preapproval period;‚Äã

135.8        (2) the number of each type of license available during the license preapproval period;‚Äã

135.9        (3) the date on which the office will begin accepting applications for license preapproval;‚Äã
135.10   and‚Äã

135.11       (4) the date on which the office will no longer accept applications.‚Äã

135.12       (b) The office must begin accepting applications no later than July 24, 2024. The‚Äã
135.13   application period must end on August 12, 2024.‚Äã

135.14       Subd. 4. Application requirements. (a) An applicant for license preapproval must:‚Äã

135.15       (1) complete an application that contains the information described in Minnesota Statutes,‚Äã
135.16   section 342.14, subdivision 1, on a form and in a manner approved by the office; and‚Äã

135.17       (2) pay the applicable application fee required under Minnesota Statutes, section 342.11,‚Äã
135.18   paragraph (b), for the license being sought.‚Äã

135.19       (b) The office shall not require an applicant for a license preapproval to identify or have‚Äã
135.20   acquired any property on which the cannabis business will operate.‚Äã

135.21       (c) If the office receives an application that fails to provide the office with the required‚Äã
135.22   information or pay the applicable application fee, the office shall issue a deficiency notice‚Äã
135.23   to the applicant that states the amount of time that the applicant has to submit the required‚Äã
135.24   information or pay the application fee to the office.‚Äã

135.25       (d) Failure by an applicant to submit all required information to the office or pay the‚Äã
135.26   application fee to the office shall result in the application being rejected.‚Äã

135.27       Subd. 5. Application review; qualified applicants. (a) The office must accept‚Äã
135.28   applications for license preapproval during the application period. As part of the application‚Äã
135.29   process, the office must verify the applicant's status as a social equity applicant.‚Äã

135.30       (b) The office may deny an application if:‚Äã

135.31       (1) the application is incomplete;‚Äã


         Article 2 Sec. 148.‚Äã                            135‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


136.1        (2) the application contains a materially false statement about the applicant or omits‚Äã
136.2    information required under Minnesota Statutes, section 342.14, subdivision 1;‚Äã

136.3        (3) the applicant does not meet the qualifications under Minnesota Statutes, section‚Äã
136.4    342.16;‚Äã

136.5        (4) the applicant is prohibited from holding the license under Minnesota Statutes, section‚Äã
136.6    342.18, subdivision 2;‚Äã

136.7        (5) the application does not meet the minimum requirements under Minnesota Statutes,‚Äã
136.8    section 342.18, subdivision 3;‚Äã

136.9        (6) the applicant fails to pay the applicable application fee to the office;‚Äã

136.10       (7) the applicant failed to submit the application to the office by the application deadline;‚Äã

136.11       (8) the applicant submitted more than one application for a license type; or‚Äã

136.12       (9) the office determines that the applicant would be prohibited from holding a license‚Äã
136.13   for any other reason.‚Äã

136.14       (c) If the office denies an application, the office must notify the applicant of the denial‚Äã
136.15   and the basis for the denial.‚Äã

136.16       (d) The office may request additional information from an applicant if the office‚Äã
136.17   determines that the information is necessary to review or process the application. If the‚Äã
136.18   applicant does not provide the additional requested information within 14 calendar days,‚Äã
136.19   the office may deny the application.‚Äã

136.20       (e) An applicant whose application is not denied under this subdivision is a qualified‚Äã
136.21   applicant.‚Äã

136.22       Subd. 6. Lottery. (a) If there are fewer license preapprovals available for a license type‚Äã
136.23   than the number of qualified applicants for that license type, the office must conduct a lottery‚Äã
136.24   to select applicants for license preapproval. The lottery must include all qualified applicants‚Äã
136.25   seeking license preapproval for the license type and must be impartial, random, and in a‚Äã
136.26   format determined by the office.‚Äã

136.27       (b) The office may remove an applicant from the lottery if the office determines that the‚Äã
136.28   applicant has violated this chapter or rules adopted pursuant to this chapter that would justify‚Äã
136.29   the revocation or nonrenewal of a license. If the office removes an applicant from a lottery,‚Äã
136.30   the office must notify the applicant of the removal and the basis for the removal.‚Äã

136.31       (c) Following the completion of any lottery conducted under this subdivision, the office‚Äã
136.32   must notify each applicant that the applicant was either selected or not selected in the lottery.‚Äã


         Article 2 Sec. 148.‚Äã                           136‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                   BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


137.1        Subd. 7. Background check; preapproval. (a) Before granting a license preapproval,‚Äã
137.2    the office may conduct a background check of a qualified applicant consistent with Minnesota‚Äã
137.3    Statutes, section 342.15.‚Äã

137.4        (b) The office must issue license preapproval to a qualified applicant if the applicant is‚Äã
137.5    not disqualified under Minnesota Statutes, section 342.15, and:‚Äã

137.6        (1) there are a sufficient number of licenses of the type the applicant is seeking for all‚Äã
137.7    qualified applicants to receive a license preapproval; or‚Äã

137.8        (2) the qualified applicant is selected in the lottery conducted under subdivision 6.‚Äã

137.9        (c) The office must notify an applicant of the results of any background check and‚Äã
137.10   whether the office has granted a license preapproval. If the office does not grant a license‚Äã
137.11   preapproval, the notice must state the specific reasons for the office's decision.‚Äã

137.12       Subd. 8. License preapproval; purpose; restrictions. (a) A license preapproval issued‚Äã
137.13   by the office is evidence that:‚Äã

137.14       (1) the applicant has submitted all necessary information to the office;‚Äã

137.15       (2) the office has determined that the applicant is qualified to hold a license of the type‚Äã
137.16   for which the license preapproval is issued; and‚Äã

137.17       (3) the office will issue the person a license after the office adopts initial rules pursuant‚Äã
137.18   to Minnesota Statutes, section 342.02, subdivision 5, unless the office revokes the license‚Äã
137.19   preapproval pursuant to subdivision 9.‚Äã

137.20       (b) Upon request by a person with a license preapproval, the office must provide‚Äã
137.21   confirmation of the license preapproval to third parties to assist the person in taking the‚Äã
137.22   steps necessary to prepare for business operations, including:‚Äã

137.23       (1) establishing legal control of the site of the cannabis business through a lease, purchase,‚Äã
137.24   or other means;‚Äã

137.25       (2) gaining zoning or planning approval from a local unit of government for the site of‚Äã
137.26   the cannabis business; and‚Äã

137.27       (3) raising capital for the person's business operations.‚Äã

137.28       (c) A person with a license preapproval is not authorized to open a cannabis business‚Äã
137.29   or engage in any activity that requires a license issued under this chapter.‚Äã

137.30       (d) A person with a license preapproval must not:‚Äã




         Article 2 Sec. 148.‚Äã                           137‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                      REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


138.1        (1) purchase, possess, cultivate, manufacture, distribute, dispense, or sell cannabis plants,‚Äã
138.2    cannabis flower, cannabis products, medical cannabis flower, or medical cannabinoid‚Äã
138.3    products;‚Äã

138.4        (2) manufacture, distribute, or sell edible cannabinoid products or lower-potency hemp‚Äã
138.5    edibles unless the person has explicit permission from the office to engage in those activities‚Äã
138.6    and has a valid license authorizing those actions or is registered pursuant to Minnesota‚Äã
138.7    Statutes, section 151.72;‚Äã

138.8        (3) make any transfer of an ownership interest that causes a change in the individual or‚Äã
138.9    entity that holds the controlling ownership interest of the cannabis business;‚Äã

138.10       (4) make any change or transfer of ownership or control that would require a new business‚Äã
138.11   registration with the secretary of state; or‚Äã

138.12       (5) make any transfer of ownership interest that causes the person with a license‚Äã
138.13   preapproval to no longer qualify as a social equity applicant under Minnesota Statutes,‚Äã
138.14   section 342.17.‚Äã

138.15       (e) The prohibitions under paragraphs (c) and (d) do not prohibit a person with a license‚Äã
138.16   preapproval from engaging in early cultivation if authorized by the office.‚Äã

138.17       Subd. 9. Revocation of preapproval. The office may revoke a license preapproval if‚Äã
138.18   the person holding the license preapproval, including any true party of interest as defined‚Äã
138.19   in Minnesota Statutes, section 342.185, subdivision 1, paragraph (g):‚Äã

138.20       (1) fraudulently or deceptively obtained a license preapproval;‚Äã

138.21       (2) fails to reveal any material fact pertaining to the qualification for a license preapproval;‚Äã

138.22       (3) violates any provision of this chapter; or‚Äã

138.23       (4) is not registered or in good standing with the Office of the Secretary of State.‚Äã

138.24       Subd. 10. Conversion of preapproval. (a) After the office adopts initial rules pursuant‚Äã
138.25   to Minnesota Statutes, section 342.02, subdivision 5, the office must issue a license to any‚Äã
138.26   person who has received a license preapproval if:‚Äã

138.27       (1) the person provides the address and legal property description of the location where‚Äã
138.28   the business will operate;‚Äã

138.29       (2) the person provides the name of the local unit of government where the business will‚Äã
138.30   be located;‚Äã




         Article 2 Sec. 148.‚Äã                             138‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                      REVISOR                 BD                H4757-4‚Äã


139.1           (3) if applicable, the person provides an updated description of the location where the‚Äã
139.2    business will operate, an updated security plan, and any other additional information required‚Äã
139.3    by the office;‚Äã

139.4           (4) the office contacts the appropriate local unit of government as provided in Minnesota‚Äã
139.5    Statutes, section 342.13, paragraph (f), to confirm that the proposed cannabis business‚Äã
139.6    complies with local zoning ordinances and, if applicable, whether the proposed business‚Äã
139.7    complies with the state fire code and building code;‚Äã

139.8           (5) the office completes an inspection of the site where the cannabis business will be‚Äã
139.9    located and approves the site; and‚Äã

139.10          (6) the person pays any applicable license fee.‚Äã

139.11          (b) The office must not grant a license to a person who has received a license preapproval‚Äã
139.12   if:‚Äã

139.13          (1) the ownership of the cannabis business has changed since the office granted a license‚Äã
139.14   preapproval and the person has not filed an updated ownership disclosure as required by‚Äã
139.15   the office;‚Äã

139.16          (2) the office confirms that the cannabis business for which the office granted a license‚Äã
139.17   preapproval does not meet local zoning and land use laws;‚Äã

139.18          (3) the person fails to submit any required information;‚Äã

139.19          (4) the person submits a materially false statement about the applicant or fails to provide‚Äã
139.20   any required information;‚Äã

139.21          (5) the person fails to pay the applicable license fee; or‚Äã

139.22          (6) the office determines that the person is disqualified from holding the license or would‚Äã
139.23   operate in violation of the provisions of this chapter.‚Äã

139.24          (d) Within 90 days of receiving the information required under paragraph (a), clauses‚Äã
139.25   (1) to (3), the office shall grant final authorization and issue the appropriate license or send‚Äã
139.26   the applicant a notice of rejection setting forth specific reasons that the office did not grant‚Äã
139.27   a license.‚Äã

139.28          Subd. 11. Applicants; right to a reconsideration. (a) If the office denies an application‚Äã
139.29   for a license preapproval or removes an applicant from a lottery, the applicant may request‚Äã
139.30   a records review of the submitted application materials within seven calendar days of‚Äã
139.31   receiving notification that the office denied the application or removed the applicant.‚Äã




         Article 2 Sec. 148.‚Äã                              139‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                     REVISOR              BD                H4757-4‚Äã


140.1        (b) Upon an applicant's request, the office must allow the applicant to examine the‚Äã
140.2    applicant's records received by the office.‚Äã

140.3        (c) A person whose license preapproval is later revoked by the office may request‚Äã
140.4    reconsideration by the director.‚Äã

140.5        (d) An applicant whose application is denied or not selected in a lottery may not appeal‚Äã
140.6    or request a hearing.‚Äã

140.7        Subd. 12. Retention of applications. The office must retain an application that was not‚Äã
140.8    selected in a lottery for one year. An application retained under this subdivision is subject‚Äã
140.9    to the requirements under Minnesota Statutes, section 342.14, subdivision 9.‚Äã

140.10       Subd. 13. Data. Data collected, created, or maintained by the office pursuant to this‚Äã
140.11   section are application data submitted by an applicant for a cannabis business license and‚Äã
140.12   are subject to Minnesota Statutes, section 342.20.‚Äã

140.13       EFFECTIVE DATE. This section is effective the day following final enactment.‚Äã


140.14     Sec. 149. THIRD-PARTY BACKGROUND CHECKS FOR LICENSE‚Äã
140.15   APPLICATIONS.‚Äã

140.16       (a) Notwithstanding Minnesota Statutes, section 342.15, until approved by the Federal‚Äã
140.17   Bureau of Investigation, the director may accept a third-party local and national criminal‚Äã
140.18   background check submitted by an applicant for a license or renewal in lieu of a‚Äã
140.19   fingerprint-based national criminal history records check. Any third-party background check‚Äã
140.20   must:‚Äã

140.21       (1) be conducted by a third-party consumer reporting agency or background screening‚Äã
140.22   company that is in compliance with the federal Fair Credit Reporting Act and accredited‚Äã
140.23   by the Professional Background Screening Association;‚Äã

140.24       (2) include a multistate and multijurisdiction criminal record locator or other similar‚Äã
140.25   commercial nationwide database with validation; and‚Äã

140.26       (3) include other background screening as the director may require.‚Äã

140.27       (b) The applicant must request a background check not more than 60 days before‚Äã
140.28   submitting the application.‚Äã

140.29       (c) Notwithstanding Minnesota Statutes, section 342.15, until approved by the Federal‚Äã
140.30   Bureau of Investigation, a license holder may use a third-party local and national criminal‚Äã
140.31   background check submitted by a cannabis worker in lieu of a fingerprint-based national‚Äã
140.32   criminal history records check. Any third-party background check must:‚Äã

141.20   the transfer shall continue to be represented by the same exclusive representative after the‚Äã
141.21   transfer;‚Äã

141.22       (3) the applicable collective bargaining agreements with exclusive representatives shall‚Äã
141.23   continue in full force and effect for such transferred employees after the transfer;‚Äã

141.25   employees about any proposed changes affecting or relating to the transferred employees'‚Äã
141.26   terms and conditions of employment to the extent such changes are not addressed in the‚Äã
141.27   applicable collective bargaining agreement; and‚Äã

141.29   Cannabis Management, the total length of time that the employee has served in the‚Äã
141.30   appointment shall include all time served in the appointment at the transferring agency and‚Äã
141.31   the time served in the appointment at the Office of Cannabis Management. An employee‚Äã
141.32   in a temporary unclassified position who was hired by a transferring agency through an‚Äã

150.14       (2) the date, time, and place of the receipt of the scrap metal or motor vehicle purchased‚Äã
150.15   or acquired and a unique transaction identifier;‚Äã

150.17   identification number;‚Äã

150.19   or acquire the scrap metal or motor vehicle;‚Äã

150.21   delivering the scrap metal or motor vehicle, including the vehicle make and model, and any‚Äã
150.22   identifying marks on the vehicle, such as a business name, decals, or markings, if applicable;‚Äã

150.24   609.48, attesting that the scrap metal or motor vehicle is not stolen and is free of any liens‚Äã
150.25   or encumbrances and the seller has the right to sell it;‚Äã

150.26       (7) a copy of the receipt, which must include at least the following information: the name‚Äã
150.27   and address of the dealer, the date and time the scrap metal or motor vehicle was received‚Äã
150.28   by the dealer, an accurate description of the scrap metal or motor vehicle, and the amount‚Äã
150.29   paid for the scrap metal or motor vehicle;‚Äã

150.30       (8) in order to purchase or acquire a detached catalytic converter, the vehicle identification‚Äã
150.31   number of the car it was removed from or, as an alternative, any numbers, bar codes, stickers,‚Äã
150.32   or other unique markings, whether resulting from the pilot project created under subdivision‚Äã

155.17                                            ARTICLE 5‚Äã
155.18                                 CONSUMER DATA POLICY‚Äã


155.19     Section 1. [13.6505] ATTORNEY GENERAL DATA CODED ELSEWHERE.‚Äã

155.20       Subdivision 1. Scope. The section referred to in this section is codified outside this‚Äã
155.21   chapter. Those sections classify attorney general data as other than public, place restrictions‚Äã
155.22   on access to government data, or involve data sharing.‚Äã

155.23       Subd. 2. Data privacy and protection assessments. A data privacy and protection‚Äã
155.24   assessment collected or maintained by the attorney general is classified under section‚Äã
155.25   325O.08.‚Äã


155.26     Sec. 2. [325O.01] CITATION.‚Äã

155.27       This chapter may be cited as the "Minnesota Consumer Data Privacy Act."‚Äã


155.28     Sec. 3. [325O.02] DEFINITIONS.‚Äã

155.29       (a) For purposes of this chapter, the following terms have the meanings given.‚Äã


         Article 5 Sec. 3.‚Äã                            155‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


156.1        (b) "Affiliate" means a legal entity that controls, is controlled by, or is under common‚Äã
156.2    control with another legal entity. For purposes of this paragraph, "control" or "controlled"‚Äã
156.3    means: ownership of or the power to vote more than 50 percent of the outstanding shares‚Äã
156.4    of any class of voting security of a company; control in any manner over the election of a‚Äã
156.5    majority of the directors or of individuals exercising similar functions; or the power to‚Äã
156.6    exercise a controlling influence over the management of a company.‚Äã

156.7        (c) "Authenticate" means to use reasonable means to determine that a request to exercise‚Äã
156.8    any of the rights under section 325O.05, subdivision 1, paragraphs (b) to (h), is being made‚Äã
156.9    by or rightfully on behalf of the consumer who is entitled to exercise the rights with respect‚Äã
156.10   to the personal data at issue.‚Äã

156.11       (d) "Biometric data" means data generated by automatic measurements of an individual's‚Äã
156.12   biological characteristics, including a fingerprint, a voiceprint, eye retinas, irises, or other‚Äã
156.13   unique biological patterns or characteristics that are used to identify a specific individual.‚Äã
156.14   Biometric data does not include:‚Äã

156.15       (1) a digital or physical photograph;‚Äã

156.16       (2) an audio or video recording; or‚Äã

156.17       (3) any data generated from a digital or physical photograph, or an audio or video‚Äã
156.18   recording, unless the data is generated to identify a specific individual.‚Äã

156.19       (e) "Child" has the meaning given in United States Code, title 15, section 6501.‚Äã

156.20       (f) "Consent" means any freely given, specific, informed, and unambiguous indication‚Äã
156.21   of the consumer's wishes by which the consumer signifies agreement to the processing of‚Äã
156.22   personal data relating to the consumer. Acceptance of a general or broad terms of use or‚Äã
156.23   similar document that contains descriptions of personal data processing along with other,‚Äã
156.24   unrelated information does not constitute consent. Hovering over, muting, pausing, or closing‚Äã
156.25   a given piece of content does not constitute consent. A consent is not valid when the‚Äã
156.26   consumer's indication has been obtained by a dark pattern. A consumer may revoke consent‚Äã
156.27   previously given, consistent with this chapter.‚Äã

156.28       (g) "Consumer" means a natural person who is a Minnesota resident acting only in an‚Äã
156.29   individual or household context. Consumer does not include a natural person acting in a‚Äã
156.30   commercial or employment context.‚Äã

156.31       (h) "Controller" means the natural or legal person who, alone or jointly with others,‚Äã
156.32   determines the purposes and means of the processing of personal data.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 3.‚Äã                             156‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                   BD                H4757-4‚Äã


157.1        (i) "Decisions that produce legal or similarly significant effects concerning the consumer"‚Äã
157.2    means decisions made by the controller that result in the provision or denial by the controller‚Äã
157.3    of financial or lending services, housing, insurance, education enrollment or opportunity,‚Äã
157.4    criminal justice, employment opportunities, health care services, or access to essential goods‚Äã
157.5    or services.‚Äã

157.6        (j) "Dark pattern" means a user interface designed or manipulated with the substantial‚Äã
157.7    effect of subverting or impairing user autonomy, decision making, or choice.‚Äã

157.8        (k) "Deidentified data" means data that cannot reasonably be used to infer information‚Äã
157.9    about or otherwise be linked to an identified or identifiable natural person or a device linked‚Äã
157.10   to an identified or identifiable natural person, provided that the controller that possesses the‚Äã
157.11   data:‚Äã

157.12       (1) takes reasonable measures to ensure that the data cannot be associated with a natural‚Äã
157.13   person;‚Äã

157.14       (2) publicly commits to process the data only in a deidentified fashion and not attempt‚Äã
157.15   to reidentify the data; and‚Äã

157.16       (3) contractually obligates any recipients of the information to comply with all provisions‚Äã
157.17   of this paragraph.‚Äã

157.18       (l) "Delete" means to remove or destroy information so that it is not maintained in human-‚Äã
157.19   or machine-readable form and cannot be retrieved or utilized in the ordinary course of‚Äã
157.20   business.‚Äã

157.21       (m) "Genetic information" has the meaning given in section 13.386, subdivision 1.‚Äã

157.22       (n) "Identified or identifiable natural person" means a person who can be readily‚Äã
157.23   identified, directly or indirectly.‚Äã

157.24       (o) "Known child" means a person under circumstances where a controller has actual‚Äã
157.25   knowledge of, or willfully disregards, that the person is under 13 years of age.‚Äã

157.26       (p) "Personal data" means any information that is linked or reasonably linkable to an‚Äã
157.27   identified or identifiable natural person. Personal data does not include deidentified data or‚Äã
157.28   publicly available information. For purposes of this paragraph, "publicly available‚Äã
157.29   information" means information that (1) is lawfully made available from federal, state, or‚Äã
157.30   local government records or widely distributed media, or (2) a controller has a reasonable‚Äã
157.31   basis to believe has lawfully been made available to the general public.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 3.‚Äã                            157‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                   BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


158.1        (q) "Process" or "processing" means any operation or set of operations that are performed‚Äã
158.2    on personal data or on sets of personal data, whether or not by automated means, including‚Äã
158.3    but not limited to the collection, use, storage, disclosure, analysis, deletion, or modification‚Äã
158.4    of personal data.‚Äã

158.5        (r) "Processor" means a natural or legal person who processes personal data on behalf‚Äã
158.6    of a controller.‚Äã

158.7        (s) "Profiling" means any form of automated processing of personal data to evaluate,‚Äã
158.8    analyze, or predict personal aspects related to an identified or identifiable natural person's‚Äã
158.9    economic situation, health, personal preferences, interests, reliability, behavior, location,‚Äã
158.10   or movements.‚Äã

158.11       (t) "Pseudonymous data" means personal data that cannot be attributed to a specific‚Äã
158.12   natural person without the use of additional information, provided that the additional‚Äã
158.13   information is kept separately and is subject to appropriate technical and organizational‚Äã
158.14   measures to ensure that the personal data are not attributed to an identified or identifiable‚Äã
158.15   natural person.‚Äã

158.16       (u) "Sale," "sell," or "sold" means the exchange of personal data for monetary or other‚Äã
158.17   valuable consideration by the controller to a third party. Sale does not include the following:‚Äã

158.18       (1) the disclosure of personal data to a processor who processes the personal data on‚Äã
158.19   behalf of the controller;‚Äã

158.20       (2) the disclosure of personal data to a third party for purposes of providing a product‚Äã
158.21   or service requested by the consumer;‚Äã

158.22       (3) the disclosure or transfer of personal data to an affiliate of the controller;‚Äã

158.23       (4) the disclosure of information that the consumer intentionally made available to the‚Äã
158.24   general public via a channel of mass media and did not restrict to a specific audience;‚Äã

158.25       (5) the disclosure or transfer of personal data to a third party as an asset that is part of a‚Äã
158.26   completed or proposed merger, acquisition, bankruptcy, or other transaction in which the‚Äã
158.27   third party assumes control of all or part of the controller's assets; or‚Äã

158.28       (6) the exchange of personal data between the producer of a good or service and‚Äã
158.29   authorized agents of the producer who sell and service the goods and services, to enable‚Äã
158.30   the cooperative provisioning of goods and services by both the producer and the producer's‚Äã
158.31   agents.‚Äã

158.32       (v) Sensitive data is a form of personal data. "Sensitive data" means:‚Äã



         Article 5 Sec. 3.‚Äã                             158‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


159.1        (1) personal data revealing racial or ethnic origin, religious beliefs, mental or physical‚Äã
159.2    health condition or diagnosis, sexual orientation, or citizenship or immigration status;‚Äã

159.3        (2) the processing of biometric data or genetic information for the purpose of uniquely‚Äã
159.4    identifying an individual;‚Äã

159.5        (3) the personal data of a known child; or‚Äã

159.6        (4) specific geolocation data.‚Äã

159.7        (w) "Specific geolocation data" means information derived from technology, including‚Äã
159.8    but not limited to global positioning system level latitude and longitude coordinates or other‚Äã
159.9    mechanisms, that directly identifies the geographic coordinates of a consumer or a device‚Äã
159.10   linked to a consumer with an accuracy of more than three decimal degrees of latitude and‚Äã
159.11   longitude or the equivalent in an alternative geographic coordinate system, or a street address‚Äã
159.12   derived from the coordinates. Specific geolocation data does not include the content of‚Äã
159.13   communications, the contents of databases containing street address information which are‚Äã
159.14   accessible to the public as authorized by law, or any data generated by or connected to‚Äã
159.15   advanced utility metering infrastructure systems or other equipment for use by a public‚Äã
159.16   utility.‚Äã

159.17       (x) "Targeted advertising" means displaying advertisements to a consumer where the‚Äã
159.18   advertisement is selected based on personal data obtained or inferred from the consumer's‚Äã
159.19   activities over time and across nonaffiliated websites or online applications to predict the‚Äã
159.20   consumer's preferences or interests. Targeted advertising does not include:‚Äã

159.21       (1) advertising based on activities within a controller's own websites or online‚Äã
159.22   applications;‚Äã

159.23       (2) advertising based on the context of a consumer's current search query or visit to a‚Äã
159.24   website or online application;‚Äã

159.25       (3) advertising to a consumer in response to the consumer's request for information or‚Äã
159.26   feedback; or‚Äã

159.27       (4) processing personal data solely for measuring or reporting advertising performance,‚Äã
159.28   reach, or frequency.‚Äã

159.29       (y) "Third party" means a natural or legal person, public authority, agency, or body other‚Äã
159.30   than the consumer, controller, processor, or an affiliate of the processor or the controller.‚Äã

159.31       (z) "Trade secret" has the meaning given in section 325C.01, subdivision 5.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 3.‚Äã                            159‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                  BD                H4757-4‚Äã


160.1      Sec. 4. [325O.03] SCOPE; EXCLUSIONS.‚Äã

160.2        Subdivision 1. Scope. (a) This chapter applies to legal entities that conduct business in‚Äã
160.3    Minnesota or produce products or services that are targeted to residents of Minnesota, and‚Äã
160.4    that satisfy one or more of the following thresholds:‚Äã

160.5        (1) during a calendar year, controls or processes personal data of 100,000 consumers or‚Äã
160.6    more, excluding personal data controlled or processed solely for the purpose of completing‚Äã
160.7    a payment transaction; or‚Äã

160.8        (2) derives over 25 percent of gross revenue from the sale of personal data and processes‚Äã
160.9    or controls personal data of 25,000 consumers or more.‚Äã

160.10       (b) A controller or processor acting as a technology provider under section 13.32 shall‚Äã
160.11   comply with this chapter and section 13.32, except that when the provisions of section 13.32‚Äã
160.12   conflict with this chapter, section 13.32 prevails.‚Äã

164.1        (b) Controllers that are in compliance with the Children's Online Privacy Protection Act,‚Äã
