164.4      Sec. 5. [325O.04] RESPONSIBILITY ACCORDING TO ROLE.‚Äã

164.5        (a) Controllers and processors are responsible for meeting the respective obligations‚Äã
164.6    established under this chapter.‚Äã

164.7        (b) Processors are responsible under this chapter for adhering to the instructions of the‚Äã
164.8    controller and assisting the controller to meet the controller's obligations under this chapter.‚Äã
164.9    Assistance under this paragraph shall include the following:‚Äã

164.10       (1) taking into account the nature of the processing, the processor shall assist the controller‚Äã
164.11   by appropriate technical and organizational measures, insofar as this is possible, for the‚Äã
164.12   fulfillment of the controller's obligation to respond to consumer requests to exercise their‚Äã
164.13   rights pursuant to section 325O.05; and‚Äã

164.14       (2) taking into account the nature of processing and the information available to the‚Äã
164.15   processor, the processor shall assist the controller in meeting the controller's obligations in‚Äã
164.16   relation to the security of processing the personal data and in relation to the notification of‚Äã
164.17   a breach of the security of the system pursuant to section 325E.61, and shall provide‚Äã
164.18   information to the controller necessary to enable the controller to conduct and document‚Äã
164.19   any data privacy and protection assessments required by section 325O.08.‚Äã

164.20       (c) A contract between a controller and a processor shall govern the processor's data‚Äã
164.21   processing procedures with respect to processing performed on behalf of the controller. The‚Äã
164.22   contract shall be binding and clearly set forth instructions for processing data, the nature‚Äã
164.23   and purpose of processing, the type of data subject to processing, the duration of processing,‚Äã
164.24   and the rights and obligations of both parties. The contract shall also require that the‚Äã
164.25   processor:‚Äã

164.26       (1) ensure that each person processing the personal data is subject to a duty of‚Äã
164.27   confidentiality with respect to the data; and‚Äã

164.28       (2) engage a subcontractor only (i) after providing the controller with an opportunity to‚Äã
164.29   object, and (ii) pursuant to a written contract in accordance with paragraph (e) that requires‚Äã
164.30   the subcontractor to meet the obligations of the processor with respect to the personal data.‚Äã

164.31       (d) Taking into account the context of processing, the controller and the processor shall‚Äã
164.32   implement appropriate technical and organizational measures to ensure a level of security‚Äã



         Article 5 Sec. 5.‚Äã                               164‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                    REVISOR                   BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


165.1    appropriate to the risk and establish a clear allocation of the responsibilities between the‚Äã
165.2    controller and the processor to implement the technical and organizational measures.‚Äã

165.3        (e) Processing by a processor shall be governed by a contract between the controller and‚Äã
165.4    the processor that is binding on both parties and that sets out the processing instructions to‚Äã
165.5    which the processor is bound, including the nature and purpose of the processing, the type‚Äã
165.6    of personal data subject to the processing, the duration of the processing, and the obligations‚Äã
165.7    and rights of both parties. The contract shall include the requirements imposed by this‚Äã
165.8    paragraph, paragraphs (c) and (d), as well as the following requirements:‚Äã

165.9        (1) at the choice of the controller, the processor shall delete or return all personal data‚Äã
165.10   to the controller as requested at the end of the provision of services, unless retention of the‚Äã
165.11   personal data is required by law;‚Äã

165.12       (2) upon a reasonable request from the controller, the processor shall make available to‚Äã
165.13   the controller all information necessary to demonstrate compliance with the obligations in‚Äã
165.14   this chapter; and‚Äã

165.15       (3) the processor shall allow for, and contribute to, reasonable assessments and inspections‚Äã
165.16   by the controller or the controller's designated assessor. Alternatively, the processor may‚Äã
165.17   arrange for a qualified and independent assessor to conduct, at least annually and at the‚Äã
165.18   processor's expense, an assessment of the processor's policies and technical and organizational‚Äã
165.19   measures in support of the obligations under this chapter. The assessor must use an‚Äã
165.20   appropriate and accepted control standard or framework and assessment procedure for‚Äã
165.21   assessments as applicable, and shall provide a report of an assessment to the controller upon‚Äã
165.22   request.‚Äã

165.23       (f) In no event shall any contract relieve a controller or a processor from the liabilities‚Äã
165.24   imposed on a controller or processor by virtue of the controller's or processor's roles in the‚Äã
165.25   processing relationship under this chapter.‚Äã

165.26       (g) Determining whether a person is acting as a controller or processor with respect to‚Äã
165.27   a specific processing of data is a fact-based determination that depends upon the context in‚Äã
165.28   which personal data are to be processed. A person that is not limited in the person's processing‚Äã
165.29   of personal data pursuant to a controller's instructions, or that fails to adhere to a controller's‚Äã
165.30   instructions, is a controller and not a processor with respect to a specific processing of data.‚Äã
165.31   A processor that continues to adhere to a controller's instructions with respect to a specific‚Äã
165.32   processing of personal data remains a processor. If a processor begins, alone or jointly with‚Äã
165.33   others, determining the purposes and means of the processing of personal data, the processor‚Äã
165.34   is a controller with respect to the processing.‚Äã


         Article 5 Sec. 5.‚Äã                              165‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                   BD                H4757-4‚Äã


166.1      Sec. 6. [325O.05] CONSUMER PERSONAL DATA RIGHTS.‚Äã

166.2        Subdivision 1. Consumer rights provided. (a) Except as provided in this chapter, a‚Äã
166.3    controller must comply with a request to exercise the consumer rights provided in this‚Äã
166.4    subdivision.‚Äã

166.5        (b) A consumer has the right to confirm whether or not a controller is processing personal‚Äã
166.6    data concerning the consumer and access the categories of personal data the controller is‚Äã
166.7    processing.‚Äã

166.8        (c) A consumer has the right to correct inaccurate personal data concerning the consumer,‚Äã
166.9    taking into account the nature of the personal data and the purposes of the processing of the‚Äã
166.10   personal data.‚Äã

166.11       (d) A consumer has the right to delete personal data concerning the consumer.‚Äã

166.12       (e) A consumer has the right to obtain personal data concerning the consumer, which‚Äã
166.13   the consumer previously provided to the controller, in a portable and, to the extent technically‚Äã
166.14   feasible, readily usable format that allows the consumer to transmit the data to another‚Äã
166.15   controller without hindrance, where the processing is carried out by automated means.‚Äã

166.16       (f) A consumer has the right to opt out of the processing of personal data concerning‚Äã
166.17   the consumer for purposes of targeted advertising, the sale of personal data, or profiling in‚Äã
166.18   furtherance of automated decisions that produce legal effects concerning a consumer or‚Äã
166.19   similarly significant effects concerning a consumer.‚Äã

166.20       (g) If a consumer's personal data is profiled in furtherance of decisions that produce‚Äã
166.21   legal effects concerning a consumer or similarly significant effects concerning a consumer,‚Äã
166.22   the consumer has the right to question the result of the profiling, to be informed of the reason‚Äã
166.23   that the profiling resulted in the decision, and, if feasible, to be informed of what actions‚Äã
166.24   the consumer might have taken to secure a different decision and the actions that the‚Äã
166.25   consumer might take to secure a different decision in the future. The consumer has the right‚Äã
166.26   to review the consumer's personal data used in the profiling. If the decision is determined‚Äã
166.27   to have been based upon inaccurate personal data, taking into account the nature of the‚Äã
166.28   personal data and the purposes of the processing of the personal data, the consumer has the‚Äã
166.29   right to have the data corrected and the profiling decision reevaluated based upon the‚Äã
166.30   corrected data.‚Äã

166.31       (h) A consumer has a right to obtain a list of the specific third parties to which the‚Äã
166.32   controller has disclosed the consumer's personal data. If the controller does not maintain‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 6.‚Äã                            166‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                  BD                H4757-4‚Äã


167.1    the information in a format specific to the consumer, a list of specific third parties to whom‚Äã
167.2    the controller has disclosed any consumers' personal data may be provided instead.‚Äã

167.3        Subd. 2. Exercising consumer rights. (a) A consumer may exercise the rights set forth‚Äã
167.4    in this section by submitting a request, at any time, to a controller specifying which rights‚Äã
167.5    the consumer wishes to exercise.‚Äã

167.6        (b) In the case of processing personal data concerning a known child, the parent or legal‚Äã
167.7    guardian of the known child may exercise the rights of this chapter on the child's behalf.‚Äã

167.8        (c) In the case of processing personal data concerning a consumer legally subject to‚Äã
167.9    guardianship or conservatorship under sections 524.5-101 to 524.5-502, the guardian or the‚Äã
167.10   conservator of the consumer may exercise the rights of this chapter on the consumer's behalf.‚Äã

167.11       (d) A consumer may designate another person as the consumer's authorized agent to‚Äã
167.12   exercise the consumer's right to opt out of the processing of the consumer's personal data‚Äã
167.13   for purposes of targeted advertising and sale under subdivision 1, paragraph (f), on the‚Äã
167.14   consumer's behalf. A consumer may designate an authorized agent by way of, among other‚Äã
167.15   things, a technology, including but not limited to an Internet link or a browser setting,‚Äã
167.16   browser extension, or global device setting, indicating the consumer's intent to opt out of‚Äã
167.17   the processing. A controller shall comply with an opt-out request received from an authorized‚Äã
167.18   agent if the controller is able to verify, with commercially reasonable effort, the identity of‚Äã
167.19   the consumer and the authorized agent's authority to act on the consumer's behalf.‚Äã

167.20       Subd. 3. Universal opt-out mechanisms. (a) A controller must allow a consumer to opt‚Äã
167.21   out of any processing of the consumer's personal data for the purposes of targeted advertising,‚Äã
167.22   or any sale of the consumer's personal data through an opt-out preference signal sent, with‚Äã
167.23   the consumer's consent, by a platform, technology, or mechanism to the controller indicating‚Äã
167.24   the consumer's intent to opt out of the processing or sale. The platform, technology, or‚Äã
167.25   mechanism must:‚Äã

167.26       (1) not unfairly disadvantage another controller;‚Äã

167.27       (2) not make use of a default setting, but require the consumer to make an affirmative,‚Äã
167.28   freely given, and unambiguous choice to opt out of the processing of the consumer's personal‚Äã
167.29   data;‚Äã

167.30       (3) be consumer-friendly and easy to use by the average consumer;‚Äã

167.31       (4) be as consistent as possible with any other similar platform, technology, or mechanism‚Äã
167.32   required by any federal or state law or regulation; and‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 6.‚Äã                            167‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


168.1          (5) enable the controller to accurately determine whether the consumer is a Minnesota‚Äã
168.2    resident and whether the consumer has made a legitimate request to opt out of any sale of‚Äã
168.3    the consumer's personal data or targeted advertising. For purposes of this paragraph, the‚Äã
168.4    use of an Internet protocol address to estimate the consumer's location is sufficient to‚Äã
168.5    determine the consumer's residence.‚Äã

168.6          (b) If a consumer's opt-out request is exercised through the platform, technology, or‚Äã
168.7    mechanism required under paragraph (a), and the request conflicts with the consumer's‚Äã
168.8    existing controller-specific privacy setting or voluntary participation in a controller's bona‚Äã
168.9    fide loyalty, rewards, premium features, discounts, or club card program, the controller‚Äã
168.10   must comply with the consumer's opt-out preference signal but may also notify the consumer‚Äã
168.11   of the conflict and provide the consumer a choice to confirm the controller-specific privacy‚Äã
168.12   setting or participation in the controller's program.‚Äã

168.13         (c) The platform, technology, or mechanism required under paragraph (a) is subject to‚Äã
168.14   the requirements of subdivision 4.‚Äã

168.15         (d) A controller that recognizes opt-out preference signals that have been approved by‚Äã
168.16   other state laws or regulations is in compliance with this subdivision.‚Äã

168.17         Subd. 4. Controller response to consumer requests. (a) Except as provided in this‚Äã
168.18   chapter, a controller must comply with a request to exercise the rights pursuant to subdivision‚Äã
168.19   1.‚Äã

168.20         (b) A controller must provide one or more secure and reliable means for consumers to‚Äã
168.21   submit a request to exercise the consumer's rights under this section. The means made‚Äã
168.22   available must take into account the ways in which consumers interact with the controller‚Äã
168.23   and the need for secure and reliable communication of the requests.‚Äã

168.24         (c) A controller may not require a consumer to create a new account in order to exercise‚Äã
168.25   a right, but a controller may require a consumer to use an existing account to exercise the‚Äã
168.26   consumer's rights under this section.‚Äã

168.27         (d) A controller must comply with a request to exercise the right in subdivision 1,‚Äã
168.28   paragraph (f), as soon as feasibly possible, but no later than 45 days of receipt of the request.‚Äã

168.29         (e) A controller must inform a consumer of any action taken on a request under‚Äã
168.30   subdivision 1 without undue delay and in any event within 45 days of receipt of the request.‚Äã
168.31   That period may be extended once by 45 additional days where reasonably necessary, taking‚Äã
168.32   into account the complexity and number of the requests. The controller must inform the‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 6.‚Äã                             168‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                       REVISOR              BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


169.1    consumer of any extension within 45 days of receipt of the request, together with the reasons‚Äã
169.2    for the delay.‚Äã

169.3        (f) If a controller does not take action on a consumer's request, the controller must inform‚Äã
169.4    the consumer without undue delay and at the latest within 45 days of receipt of the request‚Äã
169.5    of the reasons for not taking action and instructions for how to appeal the decision with the‚Äã
169.6    controller as described in subdivision 5.‚Äã

169.7        (g) Information provided under this section must be provided by the controller free of‚Äã
169.8    charge up to twice annually to the consumer. Where requests from a consumer are manifestly‚Äã
169.9    unfounded or excessive, in particular because of the repetitive character of the requests, the‚Äã
169.10   controller may either charge a reasonable fee to cover the administrative costs of complying‚Äã
169.11   with the request, or refuse to act on the request. The controller bears the burden of‚Äã
169.12   demonstrating the manifestly unfounded or excessive character of the request.‚Äã

169.13       (h) A controller is not required to comply with a request to exercise any of the rights‚Äã
169.14   under subdivision 1, paragraphs (b) to (e) and (h), if the controller is unable to authenticate‚Äã
169.15   the request using commercially reasonable efforts. In such cases, the controller may request‚Äã
169.16   the provision of additional information reasonably necessary to authenticate the request. A‚Äã
169.17   controller is not required to authenticate an opt-out request, but a controller may deny an‚Äã
169.18   opt-out request if the controller has a good faith, reasonable, and documented belief that‚Äã
169.19   the request is fraudulent. If a controller denies an opt-out request because the controller‚Äã
169.20   believes a request is fraudulent, the controller must notify the person who made the request‚Äã
169.21   that the request was denied due to the controller's belief that the request was fraudulent and‚Äã
169.22   state the controller's basis for that belief.‚Äã

169.23       (i) In response to a consumer request under subdivision 1, a controller must not disclose‚Äã
169.24   the following information about a consumer, but must instead inform the consumer with‚Äã
169.25   sufficient particularity that the controller has collected that type of information:‚Äã

169.26       (1) Social Security number;‚Äã

169.27       (2) driver's license number or other government-issued identification number;‚Äã

169.28       (3) financial account number;‚Äã

169.29       (4) health insurance account number or medical identification number;‚Äã

169.30       (5) account password, security questions, or answers; or‚Äã

169.31       (6) biometric data.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 6.‚Äã                                169‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                 REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


170.1        (j) In response to a consumer request under subdivision 1, a controller is not required‚Äã
170.2    to reveal any trade secret.‚Äã

170.3        (k) A controller that has obtained personal data about a consumer from a source other‚Äã
170.4    than the consumer may comply with a consumer's request to delete the consumer's personal‚Äã
170.5    data pursuant to subdivision 1, paragraph (d), by either:‚Äã

170.6        (1) retaining a record of the deletion request, retaining the minimum data necessary for‚Äã
170.7    the purpose of ensuring the consumer's personal data remains deleted from the business's‚Äã
170.8    records, and not using the retained data for any other purpose pursuant to the provisions of‚Äã
170.9    this chapter; or‚Äã

170.10       (2) opting the consumer out of the processing of personal data for any purpose except‚Äã
170.11   for the purposes exempted pursuant to the provisions of this chapter.‚Äã

170.12       Subd. 5. Appeal process required. (a) A controller must establish an internal process‚Äã
170.13   whereby a consumer may appeal a refusal to take action on a request to exercise any of the‚Äã
170.14   rights under subdivision 1 within a reasonable period of time after the consumer's receipt‚Äã
170.15   of the notice sent by the controller under subdivision 4, paragraph (f).‚Äã

170.16       (b) The appeal process must be conspicuously available. The process must include the‚Äã
170.17   ease of use provisions in subdivision 3 applicable to submitting requests.‚Äã

170.18       (c) Within 45 days of receipt of an appeal, a controller must inform the consumer of any‚Äã
170.19   action taken or not taken in response to the appeal, along with a written explanation of the‚Äã
170.20   reasons in support thereof. That period may be extended by 60 additional days where‚Äã
170.21   reasonably necessary, taking into account the complexity and number of the requests serving‚Äã
170.22   as the basis for the appeal. The controller must inform the consumer of any extension within‚Äã
170.23   45 days of receipt of the appeal, together with the reasons for the delay.‚Äã

170.24       (d) When informing a consumer of any action taken or not taken in response to an appeal‚Äã
170.25   pursuant to paragraph (c), the controller must provide a written explanation of the reasons‚Äã
170.26   for the controller's decision and clearly and prominently provide the consumer with‚Äã
170.27   information about how to file a complaint with the Office of the Attorney General. The‚Äã
170.28   controller must maintain records of all appeals and the controller's responses for at least 24‚Äã
170.29   months and shall, upon written request by the attorney general as part of an investigation,‚Äã
170.30   compile and provide a copy of the records to the attorney general.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 6.‚Äã                           170‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


171.1      Sec. 7. [325O.06] PROCESSING DEIDENTIFIED DATA OR PSEUDONYMOUS‚Äã
171.2    DATA.‚Äã

171.3        (a) This chapter does not require a controller or processor to do any of the following‚Äã
171.4    solely for purposes of complying with this chapter:‚Äã

171.5        (1) reidentify deidentified data;‚Äã

171.6        (2) maintain data in identifiable form, or collect, obtain, retain, or access any data or‚Äã
171.7    technology, in order to be capable of associating an authenticated consumer request with‚Äã
171.8    personal data; or‚Äã

171.9        (3) comply with an authenticated consumer request to access, correct, delete, or port‚Äã
171.10   personal data pursuant to section 325O.05, subdivision 1, if all of the following are true:‚Äã

171.11       (i) the controller is not reasonably capable of associating the request with the personal‚Äã
171.12   data, or it would be unreasonably burdensome for the controller to associate the request‚Äã
171.13   with the personal data;‚Äã

171.14       (ii) the controller does not use the personal data to recognize or respond to the specific‚Äã
171.15   consumer who is the subject of the personal data, or associate the personal data with other‚Äã
171.16   personal data about the same specific consumer; and‚Äã

171.17       (iii) the controller does not sell the personal data to any third party or otherwise‚Äã
171.18   voluntarily disclose the personal data to any third party other than a processor, except as‚Äã
171.19   otherwise permitted in this section.‚Äã

171.20       (b) The rights contained in section 325O.05, subdivision 1, paragraphs (b) to (e) and‚Äã
171.21   (h), do not apply to pseudonymous data in cases where the controller is able to demonstrate‚Äã
171.22   any information necessary to identify the consumer is kept separately and is subject to‚Äã
171.23   effective technical and organizational controls that prevent the controller from accessing‚Äã
171.24   the information.‚Äã

171.25       (c) A controller that uses pseudonymous data or deidentified data must exercise reasonable‚Äã
171.26   oversight to monitor compliance with any contractual commitments to which the‚Äã
171.27   pseudonymous data or deidentified data are subject, and must take appropriate steps to‚Äã
171.28   address any breaches of contractual commitments.‚Äã

171.29       (d) A processor or third party must not attempt to identify the subjects of deidentified‚Äã
171.30   or pseudonymous data without the express authority of the controller that caused the data‚Äã
171.31   to be deidentified or pseudonymized.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 7.‚Äã                            171‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                   BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


172.1        (e) A controller, processor, or third party must not attempt to identify the subjects of‚Äã
172.2    data that has been collected with only pseudonymous identifiers.‚Äã


172.3      Sec. 8. [325O.07] RESPONSIBILITIES OF CONTROLLERS.‚Äã

172.4        Subdivision 1. Transparency obligations. (a) Controllers must provide consumers with‚Äã
172.5    a reasonably accessible, clear, and meaningful privacy notice that includes:‚Äã

172.6        (1) the categories of personal data processed by the controller;‚Äã

172.7        (2) the purposes for which the categories of personal data are processed;‚Äã

172.8        (3) an explanation of the rights contained in section 325O.05 and how and where‚Äã
172.9    consumers may exercise those rights, including how a consumer may appeal a controller's‚Äã
172.10   action with regard to the consumer's request;‚Äã

172.11       (4) the categories of personal data that the controller sells to or shares with third parties,‚Äã
172.12   if any;‚Äã

172.13       (5) the categories of third parties, if any, with whom the controller sells or shares personal‚Äã
172.14   data;‚Äã

172.15       (6) the controller's contact information, including an active email address or other online‚Äã
172.16   mechanism that the consumer may use to contact the controller;‚Äã

172.17       (7) a description of the controller's retention policies for personal data; and‚Äã

172.18       (8) the date the privacy notice was last updated.‚Äã

172.19       (b) If a controller sells personal data to third parties, processes personal data for targeted‚Äã
172.20   advertising, or engages in profiling in furtherance of decisions that produce legal effects‚Äã
172.21   concerning a consumer or similarly significant effects concerning a consumer, the controller‚Äã
172.22   must disclose the processing in the privacy notice and provide access to a clear and‚Äã
172.23   conspicuous method outside the privacy notice for a consumer to opt out of the sale,‚Äã
172.24   processing, or profiling in furtherance of decisions that produce legal effects concerning a‚Äã
172.25   consumer or similarly significant effects concerning a consumer. This method may include‚Äã
172.26   but is not limited to an Internet hyperlink clearly labeled "Your Opt-Out Rights" or "Your‚Äã
172.27   Privacy Rights" that directly effectuates the opt-out request or takes consumers to a web‚Äã
172.28   page where the consumer can make the opt-out request.‚Äã

172.29       (c) The privacy notice must be made available to the public in each language in which‚Äã
172.30   the controller provides a product or service that is subject to the privacy notice or carries‚Äã
172.31   out activities related to the product or service.‚Äã



         Article 5 Sec. 8.‚Äã                             172‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


173.1        (d) The controller must provide the privacy notice in a manner that is reasonably‚Äã
173.2    accessible to and usable by individuals with disabilities.‚Äã

173.3        (e) Whenever a controller makes a material change to the controller's privacy notice or‚Äã
173.4    practices, the controller must notify consumers affected by the material change with respect‚Äã
173.5    to any prospectively collected personal data and provide a reasonable opportunity for‚Äã
173.6    consumers to withdraw consent to any further materially different collection, processing,‚Äã
173.7    or transfer of previously collected personal data under the changed policy. The controller‚Äã
173.8    shall take all reasonable electronic measures to provide notification regarding material‚Äã
173.9    changes to affected consumers, taking into account available technology and the nature of‚Äã
173.10   the relationship.‚Äã

173.11       (f) A controller is not required to provide a separate Minnesota-specific privacy notice‚Äã
173.12   or section of a privacy notice if the controller's general privacy notice contains all the‚Äã
173.13   information required by this section.‚Äã

173.14       (g) The privacy notice must be posted online through a conspicuous hyperlink using the‚Äã
173.15   word "privacy" on the controller's website home page or on a mobile application's app store‚Äã
173.16   page or download page. A controller that maintains an application on a mobile or other‚Äã
173.17   device shall also include a hyperlink to the privacy notice in the application's settings menu‚Äã
173.18   or in a similarly conspicuous and accessible location. A controller that does not operate a‚Äã
173.19   website shall make the privacy notice conspicuously available to consumers through a‚Äã
173.20   medium regularly used by the controller to interact with consumers, including but not limited‚Äã
173.21   to mail.‚Äã

173.22       Subd. 2. Use of data. (a) A controller must limit the collection of personal data to what‚Äã
173.23   is adequate, relevant, and reasonably necessary in relation to the purposes for which the‚Äã
173.24   data are processed, which must be disclosed to the consumer.‚Äã

173.25       (b) Except as provided in this chapter, a controller may not process personal data for‚Äã
173.26   purposes that are not reasonably necessary to, or compatible with, the purposes for which‚Äã
173.27   the personal data are processed, as disclosed to the consumer, unless the controller obtains‚Äã
173.28   the consumer's consent.‚Äã

173.29       (c) A controller shall establish, implement, and maintain reasonable administrative,‚Äã
173.30   technical, and physical data security practices to protect the confidentiality, integrity, and‚Äã
173.31   accessibility of personal data, including the maintenance of an inventory of the data that‚Äã
173.32   must be managed to exercise these responsibilities. The data security practices shall be‚Äã
173.33   appropriate to the volume and nature of the personal data at issue.‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 8.‚Äã                            173‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                    REVISOR                   BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


174.1           (d) Except as otherwise provided in this act, a controller may not process sensitive data‚Äã
174.2    concerning a consumer without obtaining the consumer's consent, or, in the case of the‚Äã
174.3    processing of personal data concerning a known child, without obtaining consent from the‚Äã
174.4    child's parent or lawful guardian, in accordance with the requirement of the Children's‚Äã
174.5    Online Privacy Protection Act, United States Code, title 15, sections 6501 to 6506, and its‚Äã
174.6    implementing regulations, rules, and exemptions.‚Äã

174.7           (e) A controller shall provide an effective mechanism for a consumer, or, in the case of‚Äã
174.8    the processing of personal data concerning a known child, the child's parent or lawful‚Äã
174.9    guardian, to revoke previously given consent under this subdivision. The mechanism provided‚Äã
174.10   shall be at least as easy as the mechanism by which the consent was previously given. Upon‚Äã
174.11   revocation of consent, a controller shall cease to process the applicable data as soon as‚Äã
174.12   practicable, but not later than 15 days after the receipt of the request.‚Äã

174.13          (f) A controller may not process the personal data of a consumer for purposes of targeted‚Äã
174.14   advertising, or sell the consumer's personal data, without the consumer's consent, under‚Äã
174.15   circumstances where the controller knows that the consumer is between the ages of 13 and‚Äã
174.16   16.‚Äã

174.17          (g) A controller may not retain personal data that is no longer relevant and reasonably‚Äã
174.18   necessary in relation to the purposes for which the data were collected and processed, unless‚Äã
174.19   retention of the data is otherwise required by law or permitted under section 325O.09.‚Äã

174.20          Subd. 3. Nondiscrimination. (a) A controller shall not process personal data on the‚Äã
174.21   basis of a consumer's or a class of consumers' actual or perceived race, color, ethnicity,‚Äã
174.22   religion, national origin, sex, gender, gender identity, sexual orientation, familial status,‚Äã
174.23   lawful source of income, or disability in a manner that unlawfully discriminates against the‚Äã
174.24   consumer or class of consumers with respect to the offering or provision of: housing,‚Äã
174.25   employment, credit, or education; or the goods, services, facilities, privileges, advantages,‚Äã
174.26   or accommodations of any place of public accommodation.‚Äã

174.27          (b) A controller may not discriminate against a consumer for exercising any of the rights‚Äã
174.28   contained in this chapter, including denying goods or services to the consumer, charging‚Äã
174.29   different prices or rates for goods or services, and providing a different level of quality of‚Äã
174.30   goods and services to the consumer. This subdivision does not: (1) require a controller to‚Äã
174.31   provide a good or service that requires the consumer's personal data that the controller does‚Äã
174.32   not collect or maintain; or (2) prohibit a controller from offering a different price, rate, level,‚Äã
174.33   quality, or selection of goods or services to a consumer, including offering goods or services‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 8.‚Äã                              174‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                  BD                H4757-4‚Äã


175.1    for no fee, if the offering is in connection with a consumer's voluntary participation in a‚Äã
175.2    bona fide loyalty, rewards, premium features, discounts, or club card program.‚Äã

175.3        Subd. 4. Waiver of rights unenforceable. Any provision of a contract or agreement of‚Äã
175.4    any kind that purports to waive or limit in any way a consumer's rights under this chapter‚Äã
175.5    is contrary to public policy and is void and unenforceable.‚Äã


175.6      Sec. 9. [325O.075] REQUIREMENTS FOR SMALL BUSINESSES.‚Äã

175.7        (a) A small business, as defined by the United States Small Business Administration‚Äã
175.8    under Code of Federal Regulations, title 13, part 121, that conducts business in Minnesota‚Äã
175.9    or produces products or services that are targeted to residents of Minnesota, must not sell‚Äã
175.10   a consumer's sensitive data without the consumer's prior consent.‚Äã

175.11       (b) Penalties and attorney general enforcement procedures under section 325O.10 apply‚Äã
175.12   to a small business that violates this section.‚Äã


175.13     Sec. 10. [325O.08] DATA PRIVACY POLICIES; DATA PRIVACY AND‚Äã
175.14   PROTECTION ASSESSMENTS.‚Äã

175.15       (a) A controller must document and maintain a description of the policies and procedures‚Äã
175.16   the controller has adopted to comply with this chapter. The description must include, where‚Äã
175.17   applicable:‚Äã

175.18       (1) the name and contact information for the controller's chief privacy officer or other‚Äã
175.19   individual with primary responsibility for directing the policies and procedures implemented‚Äã
175.20   to comply with the provisions of this chapter; and‚Äã

175.21       (2) a description of the controller's data privacy policies and procedures which reflect‚Äã
175.22   the requirements in section 325O.07, and any policies and procedures designed to:‚Äã

175.23       (i) reflect the requirements of this chapter in the design of the controller's systems;‚Äã

175.24       (ii) identify and provide personal data to a consumer as required by this chapter;‚Äã

175.25       (iii) establish, implement, and maintain reasonable administrative, technical, and physical‚Äã
175.26   data security practices to protect the confidentiality, integrity, and accessibility of personal‚Äã
175.27   data, including the maintenance of an inventory of the data that must be managed to exercise‚Äã
175.28   the responsibilities under this item;‚Äã

175.29       (iv) limit the collection of personal data to what is adequate, relevant, and reasonably‚Äã
175.30   necessary in relation to the purposes for which the data are processed;‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 10.‚Äã                            175‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                   REVISOR                  BD                 H4757-4‚Äã


176.1        (v) prevent the retention of personal data that is no longer relevant and reasonably‚Äã
176.2    necessary in relation to the purposes for which the data were collected and processed, unless‚Äã
176.3    retention of the data is otherwise required by law or permitted under section 325O.09; and‚Äã

176.4        (vi) identify and remediate violations of this chapter.‚Äã

176.5        (b) A controller must conduct and document a data privacy and protection assessment‚Äã
176.6    for each of the following processing activities involving personal data:‚Äã

176.7        (1) the processing of personal data for purposes of targeted advertising;‚Äã

176.8        (2) the sale of personal data;‚Äã

176.9        (3) the processing of sensitive data;‚Äã

176.10       (4) any processing activities involving personal data that present a heightened risk of‚Äã
176.11   harm to consumers; and‚Äã

176.12       (5) the processing of personal data for purposes of profiling, where the profiling presents‚Äã
176.13   a reasonably foreseeable risk of:‚Äã

176.14       (i) unfair or deceptive treatment of, or disparate impact on, consumers;‚Äã

176.15       (ii) financial, physical, or reputational injury to consumers;‚Äã

176.16       (iii) a physical or other intrusion upon the solitude or seclusion, or the private affairs or‚Äã
176.17   concerns, of consumers, where the intrusion would be offensive to a reasonable person; or‚Äã

176.18       (iv) other substantial injury to consumers.‚Äã

176.19       (c) A data privacy and protection assessment must take into account the type of personal‚Äã
176.20   data to be processed by the controller, including the extent to which the personal data are‚Äã
176.21   sensitive data, and the context in which the personal data are to be processed.‚Äã

176.22       (d) A data privacy and protection assessment must identify and weigh the benefits that‚Äã
176.23   may flow directly and indirectly from the processing to the controller, consumer, other‚Äã
176.24   stakeholders, and the public against the potential risks to the rights of the consumer associated‚Äã
176.25   with the processing, as mitigated by safeguards that can be employed by the controller to‚Äã
176.26   reduce the potential risks. The use of deidentified data and the reasonable expectations of‚Äã
176.27   consumers, as well as the context of the processing and the relationship between the controller‚Äã
176.28   and the consumer whose personal data will be processed, must be factored into this‚Äã
176.29   assessment by the controller.‚Äã

176.30       (e) A data privacy and protection assessment must include the description of policies‚Äã
176.31   and procedures required by paragraph (a).‚Äã



         Article 5 Sec. 10.‚Äã                            176‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                     REVISOR               BD                H4757-4‚Äã


177.1        (f) As part of a civil investigative demand, the attorney general may request, in writing,‚Äã
177.2    that a controller disclose any data privacy and protection assessment that is relevant to an‚Äã
177.3    investigation conducted by the attorney general. The controller must make a data privacy‚Äã
177.4    and protection assessment available to the attorney general upon a request made under this‚Äã
177.5    paragraph. The attorney general may evaluate the data privacy and protection assessments‚Äã
177.6    for compliance with this chapter. Data privacy and protection assessments are classified as‚Äã
177.7    nonpublic data, as defined by section 13.02, subdivision 9. The disclosure of a data privacy‚Äã
177.8    and protection assessment pursuant to a request from the attorney general under this‚Äã
177.9    paragraph does not constitute a waiver of the attorney-client privilege or work product‚Äã
177.10   protection with respect to the assessment and any information contained in the assessment.‚Äã

177.11       (g) Data privacy and protection assessments or risk assessments conducted by a controller‚Äã
177.12   for the purpose of compliance with other laws or regulations may qualify under this section‚Äã
177.13   if the assessments have a similar scope and effect.‚Äã

177.14       (h) A single data protection assessment may address multiple sets of comparable‚Äã
177.15   processing operations that include similar activities.‚Äã


177.16     Sec. 11. [325O.09] LIMITATIONS AND APPLICABILITY.‚Äã

177.17       (a) The obligations imposed on controllers or processors under this chapter do not restrict‚Äã
177.18   a controller's or a processor's ability to:‚Äã

177.19       (1) comply with federal, state, or local laws, rules, or regulations, including but not‚Äã
177.20   limited to data retention requirements in state or federal law notwithstanding a consumer's‚Äã
177.21   request to delete personal data;‚Äã

177.22       (2) comply with a civil, criminal, or regulatory inquiry, investigation, subpoena, or‚Äã
177.23   summons by federal, state, local, or other governmental authorities;‚Äã

177.24       (3) cooperate with law enforcement agencies concerning conduct or activity that the‚Äã
177.25   controller or processor reasonably and in good faith believes may violate federal, state, or‚Äã
177.26   local laws, rules, or regulations;‚Äã

177.27       (4) investigate, establish, exercise, prepare for, or defend legal claims;‚Äã

177.28       (5) provide a product or service specifically requested by a consumer; perform a contract‚Äã
177.29   to which the consumer is a party, including fulfilling the terms of a written warranty; or‚Äã
177.30   take steps at the request of the consumer prior to entering into a contract;‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 11.‚Äã                             177‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                    REVISOR                   BD                H4757-4‚Äã


178.1        (6) take immediate steps to protect an interest that is essential for the life or physical‚Äã
178.2    safety of the consumer or of another natural person, and where the processing cannot be‚Äã
178.3    manifestly based on another legal basis;‚Äã

178.4        (7) prevent, detect, protect against, or respond to security incidents, identity theft, fraud,‚Äã
178.5    harassment, malicious or deceptive activities, or any illegal activity; preserve the integrity‚Äã
178.6    or security of systems; or investigate, report, or prosecute those responsible for any such‚Äã
178.7    action;‚Äã

178.8        (8) assist another controller, processor, or third party with any of the obligations under‚Äã
178.9    this paragraph;‚Äã

178.10       (9) engage in public or peer-reviewed scientific, historical, or statistical research in the‚Äã
178.11   public interest that adheres to all other applicable ethics and privacy laws and is approved,‚Äã
178.12   monitored, and governed by an institutional review board, human subjects research ethics‚Äã
178.13   review board, or a similar independent oversight entity that has determined:‚Äã

178.14       (i) the research is likely to provide substantial benefits that do not exclusively accrue to‚Äã
178.15   the controller;‚Äã

178.16       (ii) the expected benefits of the research outweigh the privacy risks; and‚Äã

178.17       (iii) the controller has implemented reasonable safeguards to mitigate privacy risks‚Äã
178.18   associated with research, including any risks associated with reidentification; or‚Äã

178.19       (10) process personal data for the benefit of the public in the areas of public health,‚Äã
178.20   community health, or population health, but only to the extent that the processing is:‚Äã

178.21       (i) subject to suitable and specific measures to safeguard the rights of the consumer‚Äã
178.22   whose personal data is being processed; and‚Äã

178.23       (ii) under the responsibility of a professional individual who is subject to confidentiality‚Äã
178.24   obligations under federal, state, or local law.‚Äã

178.25       (b) The obligations imposed on controllers or processors under this chapter do not restrict‚Äã
178.26   a controller's or processor's ability to collect, use, or retain data to:‚Äã

178.27       (1) effectuate a product recall or identify and repair technical errors that impair existing‚Äã
178.28   or intended functionality;‚Äã

178.29       (2) perform internal operations that are reasonably aligned with the expectations of the‚Äã
178.30   consumer based on the consumer's existing relationship with the controller, or are otherwise‚Äã
178.31   compatible with processing in furtherance of the provision of a product or service specifically‚Äã




         Article 5 Sec. 11.‚Äã                             178‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                    REVISOR                   BD                H4757-4‚Äã


179.1    requested by a consumer or the performance of a contract to which the consumer is a party;‚Äã
179.2    or‚Äã

179.3          (3) conduct internal research to develop, improve, or repair products, services, or‚Äã
179.4    technology.‚Äã

179.5          (c) The obligations imposed on controllers or processors under this chapter do not apply‚Äã
179.6    where compliance by the controller or processor with this chapter would violate an‚Äã
179.7    evidentiary privilege under Minnesota law and do not prevent a controller or processor from‚Äã
179.8    providing personal data concerning a consumer to a person covered by an evidentiary‚Äã
179.9    privilege under Minnesota law as part of a privileged communication.‚Äã

179.10         (d) A controller or processor that discloses personal data to a third-party controller or‚Äã
179.11   processor in compliance with the requirements of this chapter is not in violation of this‚Äã
179.12   chapter if the recipient processes the personal data in violation of this chapter, provided that‚Äã
179.13   at the time of disclosing the personal data, the disclosing controller or processor did not‚Äã
179.14   have actual knowledge that the recipient intended to commit a violation. A third-party‚Äã
179.15   controller or processor receiving personal data from a controller or processor in compliance‚Äã
179.16   with the requirements of this chapter is not in violation of this chapter for the obligations‚Äã
179.17   of the controller or processor from which the third-party controller or processor receives‚Äã
179.18   the personal data.‚Äã

179.19         (e) Obligations imposed on controllers and processors under this chapter shall not:‚Äã

179.20         (1) adversely affect the rights or freedoms of any persons, including exercising the right‚Äã
179.21   of free speech pursuant to the First Amendment of the United States Constitution; or‚Äã

179.22         (2) apply to the processing of personal data by a natural person in the course of a purely‚Äã
179.23   personal or household activity.‚Äã

179.24         (f) Personal data that are processed by a controller pursuant to this section may be‚Äã
179.25   processed solely to the extent that the processing is:‚Äã

179.26         (1) necessary, reasonable, and proportionate to the purposes listed in this section;‚Äã

179.27         (2) adequate, relevant, and limited to what is necessary in relation to the specific purpose‚Äã
179.28   or purposes listed in this section; and‚Äã

179.29         (3) insofar as possible, taking into account the nature and purpose of processing the‚Äã
179.30   personal data, subjected to reasonable administrative, technical, and physical measures to‚Äã
179.31   protect the confidentiality, integrity, and accessibility of the personal data, and to reduce‚Äã
179.32   reasonably foreseeable risks of harm to consumers.‚Äã



         Article 5 Sec. 11.‚Äã                             179‚Äã
         HF4757 FOURTH ENGROSSMENT‚Äã                  REVISOR                   BD                  H4757-4‚Äã


180.1        (g) If a controller processes personal data pursuant to an exemption in this section, the‚Äã
180.2    controller bears the burden of demonstrating that the processing qualifies for the exemption‚Äã
180.3    and complies with the requirements in paragraph (f).‚Äã

180.4        (h) Processing personal data solely for the purposes expressly identified in paragraph‚Äã
180.5    (a), clauses (1) to (7), does not, by itself, make an entity a controller with respect to the‚Äã
180.6    processing.‚Äã


180.7      Sec. 12. [325O.10] ATTORNEY GENERAL ENFORCEMENT.‚Äã

180.8        (a) In the event that a controller or processor violates this chapter, the attorney general,‚Äã
180.9    prior to filing an enforcement action under paragraph (b), must provide the controller or‚Äã
180.10   processor with a warning letter identifying the specific provisions of this chapter the attorney‚Äã
180.11   general alleges have been or are being violated. If, after 30 days of issuance of the warning‚Äã
180.12   letter, the attorney general believes the controller or processor has failed to cure any alleged‚Äã
180.13   violation, the attorney general may bring an enforcement action under paragraph (b). This‚Äã
180.14   paragraph expires January 31, 2026.‚Äã

180.15       (b) The attorney general may bring a civil action against a controller or processor to‚Äã
180.16   enforce a provision of this chapter in accordance with section 8.31. If the state prevails in‚Äã
180.17   an action to enforce this chapter, the state may, in addition to penalties provided by paragraph‚Äã
180.18   (c) or other remedies provided by law, be allowed an amount determined by the court to be‚Äã
180.19   the reasonable value of all or part of the state's litigation expenses incurred.‚Äã

180.20       (c) Any controller or processor that violates this chapter is subject to an injunction and‚Äã
180.21   liable for a civil penalty of not more than $7,500 for each violation.‚Äã

180.22       (d) Nothing in this chapter establishes a private right of action, including under section‚Äã
180.23   8.31, subdivision 3a, for a violation of this chapter or any other law.‚Äã


180.24     Sec. 13. [325O.11] PREEMPTION OF LOCAL LAW; SEVERABILITY.‚Äã

180.25       (a) This chapter supersedes and preempts laws, ordinances, regulations, or the equivalent‚Äã
180.26   adopted by any local government regarding the processing of personal data by controllers‚Äã
180.27   or processors.‚Äã

180.28       (b) If any provision of this chapter or the chapter's application to any person or‚Äã
180.29   circumstance is held invalid, the remainder of the chapter or the application of the provision‚Äã
180.30   to other persons or circumstances is not affected.‚Äã

    152.22 DEFINITIONS.‚Äã
     Subd. 3. Disqualifying felony offense. "Disqualifying felony offense" means a violation of a‚Äã
state or federal controlled substance law that is a felony under Minnesota law, or would be a felony‚Äã
if committed in Minnesota, regardless of the sentence imposed, unless the commissioner determines‚Äã
that the person's conviction was for the medical use of cannabis or assisting with the medical use‚Äã
of cannabis.‚Äã
  152.36 IMPACT ASSESSMENT OF MEDICAL CANNABIS THERAPEUTIC‚Äã
RESEARCH.‚Äã
    Subdivision 1. Task force on medical cannabis therapeutic research. (a) A 23-member task‚Äã
force on medical cannabis therapeutic research is created to conduct an impact assessment of medical‚Äã
cannabis therapeutic research. The task force shall consist of the following members:‚Äã
    (1) two members of the house of representatives, one selected by the speaker of the house, the‚Äã
other selected by the minority leader;‚Äã
   (2) two members of the senate, one selected by the majority leader, the other selected by the‚Äã
minority leader;‚Äã
     (3) four members representing consumers or patients enrolled in the registry program, including‚Äã
at least two parents of patients under age 18;‚Äã
    (4) four members representing health care providers, including one licensed pharmacist;‚Äã
   (5) four members representing law enforcement, one from the Minnesota Chiefs of Police‚Äã
Association, one from the Minnesota Sheriff's Association, one from the Minnesota Police and‚Äã
Peace Officers Association, and one from the Minnesota County Attorneys Association;‚Äã
    (6) four members representing substance use disorder treatment providers; and‚Äã
    (7) the commissioners of health, human services, and public safety.‚Äã
    (b) Task force members listed under paragraph (a), clauses (3), (4), (5), and (6), shall be appointed‚Äã
by the governor under the appointment process in section 15.0597. Members shall serve on the task‚Äã
force at the pleasure of the appointing authority. All members must be appointed by July 15, 2014,‚Äã
and the commissioner of health shall convene the first meeting of the task force by August 1, 2014.‚Äã
     (c) There shall be two cochairs of the task force chosen from the members listed under paragraph‚Äã
(a). One cochair shall be selected by the speaker of the house and the other cochair shall be selected‚Äã
by the majority leader of the senate. The authority to convene meetings shall alternate between the‚Äã
cochairs.‚Äã
    (d) Members of the task force other than those in paragraph (a), clauses (1), (2), and (7), shall‚Äã
receive expenses as provided in section 15.059, subdivision 6.‚Äã
   Subd. 1a. Administration. The commissioner of health shall provide administrative and technical‚Äã
support to the task force.‚Äã
    Subd. 2. Impact assessment. The task force shall hold hearings to evaluate the impact of the‚Äã
use of medical cannabis and hemp and Minnesota's activities involving medical cannabis and hemp,‚Äã
including, but not limited to:‚Äã
    (1) program design and implementation;‚Äã
    (2) the impact on the health care provider community;‚Äã
    (3) patient experiences;‚Äã
    (4) the impact on the incidence of substance abuse;‚Äã
    (5) access to and quality of medical cannabis, hemp, and medical cannabis products;‚Äã
    (6) the impact on law enforcement and prosecutions;‚Äã
    (7) public awareness and perception; and‚Äã
    (8) any unintended consequences.‚Äã
    Subd. 3. Cost assessment. By January 15 of each year, beginning January 15, 2015, and ending‚Äã
January 15, 2019, the commissioners of state departments impacted by the medical cannabis‚Äã
therapeutic research study shall report to the cochairs of the task force on the costs incurred by each‚Äã

                                                   1R‚Äã
                                         APPENDIX‚Äã
                              Repealed Minnesota Statutes: H4757-4‚Äã


department on implementing sections 152.22 to 152.37. The reports must compare actual costs to‚Äã
the estimated costs of implementing these sections and must be submitted to the task force on‚Äã
medical cannabis therapeutic research.‚Äã
    Subd. 4. Reports to the legislature. (a) The cochairs of the task force shall submit the following‚Äã
reports to the chairs and ranking minority members of the legislative committees and divisions with‚Äã
jurisdiction over health and human services, public safety, judiciary, and civil law:‚Äã
   (1) by February 1, 2015, a report on the design and implementation of the registry program;‚Äã
and every two years thereafter, a complete impact assessment report; and‚Äã
    (2) upon receipt of a cost assessment from a commissioner of a state agency, the completed‚Äã
cost assessment.‚Äã
   (b) The task force may make recommendations to the legislature on whether to add or remove‚Äã
conditions from the list of qualifying medical conditions.‚Äã
   Subd. 5. No expiration. The task force on medical cannabis therapeutic research does not expire.‚Äã
   342.01 DEFINITIONS.‚Äã
   Subd. 28. Division of Medical Cannabis. "Division of Medical Cannabis" means a division‚Äã
housed in the Office of Cannabis Management that operates the medical cannabis program.‚Äã
   Subd. 53. Medical cannabis business. "Medical cannabis business" means an entity licensed‚Äã
under this chapter to engage in one or more of the following:‚Äã
   (1) the cultivation of cannabis plants for medical cannabis flower;‚Äã
   (2) the manufacture of medical cannabinoid products; and‚Äã
   (3) the retail sale of medical cannabis flower and medical cannabinoid products.‚Äã
   Subd. 55. Medical cannabis paraphernalia. "Medical cannabis paraphernalia" means a delivery‚Äã
device, related supply, or educational material used by a patient enrolled in the registry program to‚Äã
administer medical cannabis and medical cannabinoid products.‚Äã
   342.18 LICENSE SELECTION CRITERIA.‚Äã
    Subdivision 1. Market stability. The office shall issue the necessary number of licenses in‚Äã
order to ensure the sufficient supply of cannabis flower and cannabis products to meet demand,‚Äã
provide market stability, ensure a competitive market, and limit the sale of unregulated cannabis‚Äã
flower and cannabis products.‚Äã
  342.27 RETAIL SALE OF CANNABIS FLOWER AND PRODUCTS; GENERAL‚Äã
REQUIREMENTS.‚Äã
    Subd. 13. Adult-use and medical cannabis; colocation. (a) A cannabis business with a license‚Äã
or endorsement authorizing the retail sale of adult-use cannabis flower or adult-use cannabis products‚Äã
that is also a licensed medical cannabis retailer may sell medical cannabis flower and medical‚Äã
cannabinoid products on a portion of the business's premises.‚Äã
   (b) The premises must provide an appropriate space for a pharmacist employee of the medical‚Äã
cannabis retailer to consult with a patient to determine the proper type of medical cannabis flower‚Äã
and medical cannabinoid products and proper dosage for the patient.‚Äã
   342.29 CANNABIS MEZZOBUSINESS LICENSING AND OPERATIONS.‚Äã
    Subd. 9. Medical cannabis endorsement. A cannabis mezzobusiness that cultivates cannabis‚Äã
plants for use as medical cannabis flower or for use in medical cannabinoid products, processes‚Äã
medical cannabinoid products, or both, must comply with sections 342.49, paragraph (d); 342.50,‚Äã
paragraph (c), and any additional requirements established by the office.‚Äã
   342.47 MEDICAL CANNABIS BUSINESS LICENSES.‚Äã
   Subdivision 1. License types. (a) The office shall issue the following types of medical cannabis‚Äã
business licenses:‚Äã
   (1) medical cannabis cultivator;‚Äã
   (2) medical cannabis processor;‚Äã
   (3) medical cannabis retailer; and‚Äã

                                                 2R‚Äã
                                          APPENDIX‚Äã
                               Repealed Minnesota Statutes: H4757-4‚Äã


    (4) medical cannabis combination business license.‚Äã
   (b) The Division of Medical Cannabis may oversee the licensing and regulation of medical‚Äã
cannabis businesses.‚Äã
    Subd. 2. Multiple licenses; limits. (a) Except as provided in subdivision 3, a person, cooperative,‚Äã
or business holding:‚Äã
    (1) a medical cannabis cultivator license may also hold a medical cannabis processor license,‚Äã
a cannabis cultivator license, a cannabis manufacturer license, and a cannabis event organizer license‚Äã
subject to the ownership limitations that apply to those licenses;‚Äã
    (2) a medical cannabis processor license may also hold a medical cannabis cultivator license,‚Äã
a cannabis cultivator license, a cannabis manufacturer license, and a cannabis event organizer license‚Äã
subject to the ownership limitations that apply to those licenses; or‚Äã
   (3) a medical cannabis retailer license may also hold a cannabis mezzobusiness license, a‚Äã
cannabis retailer license, a cannabis delivery service license, and a cannabis event organizer license‚Äã
subject to the ownership limitations that apply to those licenses.‚Äã
   (b) Except as provided in paragraph (a), no person, cooperative, or business holding a medical‚Äã
cannabis license may own or operate any other cannabis business or hemp business.‚Äã
    (c) The office by rule may limit the number of medical cannabis business licenses that a person‚Äã
or business may hold.‚Äã
    (d) For purposes of this subdivision, a restriction on the number of licenses or type of license‚Äã
that a business may hold applies to every cooperative member or every director, manager, and‚Äã
general partner of a medical cannabis business.‚Äã
   Subd. 3. Medical cannabis combination business license. (a) A person, cooperative, or business‚Äã
holding a medical cannabis combination license is prohibited from owning or operating any other‚Äã
cannabis business or hemp business.‚Äã
    (b) A person or business may only hold one medical cannabis combination license.‚Äã
    342.48 MEDICAL CANNABIS BUSINESS APPLICATIONS.‚Äã
    In addition to the information required to be submitted under section 342.14, subdivision 1, and‚Äã
rules adopted pursuant to that section, a person, cooperative, or business seeking a medical cannabis‚Äã
business license must submit the following information in a form approved by the office:‚Äã
    (1) for medical cannabis cultivator license applicants:‚Äã
    (i) an operating plan demonstrating the proposed size and layout of the cultivation facility; plans‚Äã
for wastewater and waste disposal for the cultivation facility; plans for providing electricity, water,‚Äã
and other utilities necessary for the normal operation of the cultivation facility; and plans for‚Äã
compliance with applicable building code and federal and state environmental and workplace safety‚Äã
requirements;‚Äã
    (ii) a cultivation plan demonstrating the proposed size and layout of the cultivation facility that‚Äã
will be used exclusively for cultivation for medical cannabis, including the total amount of plant‚Äã
canopy; and‚Äã
    (iii) evidence that the business will comply with the applicable operation requirements for the‚Äã
license being sought;‚Äã
    (2) for medical cannabis processor license applicants:‚Äã
    (i) an operating plan demonstrating the proposed layout of the facility, including a diagram of‚Äã
ventilation and filtration systems; plans for wastewater and waste disposal for the manufacturing‚Äã
facility; plans for providing electricity, water, and other utilities necessary for the normal operation‚Äã
of the manufacturing facility; and plans for compliance with applicable building code and federal‚Äã
and state environmental and workplace safety requirements;‚Äã
   (ii) all methods of extraction and concentration that the applicant intends to use and the volatile‚Äã
chemicals, if any, that are involved in extraction or concentration;‚Äã
    (iii) if the applicant is seeking an endorsement to manufacture products infused with cannabinoids‚Äã
for consumption by patients enrolled in the registry program, proof of an edible cannabinoid product‚Äã
handler endorsement from the office; and‚Äã


                                                  3R‚Äã

                               Repealed Minnesota Statutes: H4757-4‚Äã


    (iv) evidence that the applicant will comply with the applicable operation requirements for the‚Äã

    (3) for medical cannabis retailer license applicants:‚Äã
    (i) a list of every retail license held by the applicant and, if the applicant is a business, every‚Äã

3; and 342.32, subdivision 3.‚Äã
    342.49 MEDICAL CANNABIS CULTIVATORS.‚Äã
    (a) A medical cannabis cultivator license entitles the license holder to grow cannabis plants‚Äã
within the approved amount of space up to 60,000 square feet of plant canopy from seed or immature‚Äã
plant to mature plant, harvest cannabis flower from a mature plant, package and label cannabis‚Äã
flower as medical cannabis flower, sell medical cannabis flower to medical cannabis processors‚Äã
and medical cannabis retailers, transport medical cannabis flower to a medical cannabis processor‚Äã
located on the same premises, and perform other actions approved by the office.‚Äã
   (b) A medical cannabis cultivator license holder must comply with all requirements of section‚Äã
342.25.‚Äã
    (c) A medical cannabis cultivator license holder must verify that every batch of medical cannabis‚Äã
flower has passed safety, potency, and consistency testing at a cannabis testing facility approved‚Äã
by the office for the testing of medical cannabis flower before the medical cannabis cultivator may‚Äã
package, label, or sell the medical cannabis flower to any other entity.‚Äã
     (d) A medical cannabis cultivator may exceed the limit of 60,000 square feet of plant canopy‚Äã
if it was legally cultivating medical cannabis with a greater plant canopy as of April 1, 2023.‚Äã
    342.50 MEDICAL CANNABIS PROCESSORS.‚Äã
   (a) A medical cannabis processor license, consistent with the specific license endorsement or‚Äã
endorsements, entitles the license holder to:‚Äã
   (1) purchase medical cannabis flower, medical cannabinoid products, hemp plant parts, and‚Äã
hemp concentrate from medical cannabis cultivators and other medical cannabis processors;‚Äã
    (2) purchase hemp plant parts from industrial hemp growers;‚Äã
    (3) make cannabis concentrate from medical cannabis flower;‚Äã
   (4) make hemp concentrate, including hemp concentrate with a delta-9 tetrahydrocannabinol‚Äã
concentration of more than 0.3 percent as measured by weight;‚Äã
    (5) manufacture medical cannabinoid products;‚Äã
   (6) package and label medical cannabinoid products for sale to other medical cannabis processors‚Äã
and to medical cannabis retailers; and‚Äã
    (7) perform other actions approved by the office.‚Äã
   (b) A medical cannabis processor license holder must comply with all requirements of section‚Äã
342.26, including requirements to obtain specific license endorsements.‚Äã
   (c) A medical cannabis processor license holder must verify that every batch of medical‚Äã
cannabinoid product has passed safety, potency, and consistency testing at a cannabis testing facility‚Äã


                                                   4R‚Äã
                                        APPENDIX‚Äã
                             Repealed Minnesota Statutes: H4757-4‚Äã


approved by the office for the testing of medical cannabinoid products before the medical cannabis‚Äã
processor may package, label, or sell the medical cannabinoid product to any other entity.‚Äã
   342.52 PATIENT REGISTRY PROGRAM.‚Äã
   Subd. 8. Allowable delivery methods. A patient in the registry program may receive medical‚Äã
cannabis flower and medical cannabinoid products. The office may approve additional delivery‚Äã
methods to expand the types of products that qualify as medical cannabinoid products.‚Äã
